Refutation of Ibn Sina's Argument for Pre-Eternal Matter
Refutation of Ibn Sina's argument for pre-eternal matter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Sina's argument that every temporal event requires pre-existing matter, and the author's refutation showing that possibility and priority are mental, not material.

Core Idea
Possibility does not require matter; priority is only in the mind.

Ibn Sina, following Aristotle, argued that the world's temporal origination would require an infinite regress of matter. The author responds by redefining the nature of possibility and priority, showing they are mental considerations. This lesson presents both the challenge and the orthodox response.

Guided Path
1
Read the sophism
Carefully read the passage presenting Ibn Sina's argument (shubha). Identify the key premises: every temporal event requires possibility, possibility requires matter, matter requires time, leading to infinite regress or a necessary being.
Note the conclusion that this argument led the Mu'tazila to consider non-existence as a thing.
2
Trace the inherent problem
Understand why the argument seems compelling: if possibility is a real capacity, it must inhere in something, and that something is matter, which is temporal.
3
Examine the author's answer
Read the answer (jawab). Note how the author redefines 'origination from non-existence' as simply having a beginning, not requiring prior matter. The possibility is a mental estimation.
Pay attention to the example of the human soul.
4
Distinguish types of priority
The author explains that the priority of possibility over the temporal existent is only a priority in the mind (essential priority), not temporal priority. Understand the difference.
This is the key refutation: the prior possibility is not temporally prior.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة أخرى : قال ابن سينا حكاية عن أرسطاطاليس : كل حادث عن عدم أمر فإنه يسبقه إمكان الوجود ضرورة، وإمكان الوجود ليس هو عدما محضاً، بل هو ما له صلاحية الوجود والعدم، ولن يتصور ذلك إلا في مادة، فكل حادث فإنه يسبقه مادة ثم تلك المادة المتقدمة لا تتصور إلا في زمان ؛ لأن قبل ومع لا يتحقق إلا في زمان والمعدوم قبل هو المعدوم مع ، وليس الإمكان قبل هو الذي يقارن الوجود، فهو إذا متقدم تقدمًا زمانيا، والعالم لو كان حادثا عن عدم لتقدمه إمكان الوجود في مادة تقدما زمانيا ، فهو إما أن يتسلسل فهو باطل، وإما أن يقف على حد لا يسبقه إمكان فلا يسبقه عدم فيكون واجبًا بغيره وهو ما ذهبنا إليه، وهذه الشبهة التي أوقعت المعتزلة في اعتقاد كون المعدوم شيئًا، وعن هذا قصروا الشيئية في الممكن وجوده إلا المستحيل ثبوته.

والجواب : أنا قد بينا أن معنى الحدوث عن عدم أنه هو الموجود الذي له أول لا الإمكان السابق عليه ليس يرجع إلى ذات هو شيء حتى يحتاج إلى مادة، بل هو أمر راجع إلى التقدير الذهني ؛ لأن ما لا يجوز وجوده لا يتحقق له ثبوت وحدوث والقبلية والمعية راجعة أيضًا إلى التقدير العقلي، وإنما نتصور نحن من حدوث العالم ما يتصورونه من حدوث النفس الإنسانية حادثة لها أول لا عن شيء، حتى يمكن أن يقال : إنها مسبوقة بالعدم ؛ أي: لم تكن فكانت وهي ممكنة الوجود في ذاتها، وإمكانها لا يستدعي مادة تسبقها ، فإن ذلك يؤدي إلى أن يكون وجودها ماديًا، فعلم أن الإمكان من حيث هو إمكان ليس يستدعي مادة وسبقه علي الموجود الحادث ليس إلا سبقا في الذهن سميتموه سبقاً ذاتياً، وذلك السبق ليس سبقا زمانيا.
Another sophism: Ibn Sina, reporting from Aristotle, said: Every temporal event from non-existence is necessarily preceded by the possibility of existence, and the possibility of existence is not pure non-existence, but rather that which has the capacity for existence and non-existence, and that cannot be conceived except in matter. So every temporal event is preceded by matter, then that preceding matter cannot be conceived except in time, because 'before' and 'with' are only realized in time, and the non-existent before is the non-existent with. And the possibility before is not that which accompanies existence. So it is temporally prior. And if the world were temporally originated from non-existence, then it would be preceded by the possibility of existence in matter temporally. Then either it leads to infinite regress, which is false, or it stops at a limit that is not preceded by possibility, so it is not preceded by non-existence, and thus it is necessary by another, which is what we hold. And this sophism is what led the Mu'tazila to believe that non-existence is a thing, and for this reason they restricted thingness to the possible existent except the impossible.

The answer: We have already explained that the meaning of temporal origination from non-existence is that it is an existent that has a beginning, but the possibility preceding it does not refer to an essence that is a thing so that it needs matter. Rather, it is a matter referring to mental estimation. For what does not allow existence does not have actuality and origination. And priority and simultaneity also refer to intellectual estimation. Indeed, we conceive of the temporal origination of the world as they conceive of the temporal origination of the human soul: it comes into existence with a beginning not from something, so that it can be said that it is preceded by non-existence, i.e., it was not and then it was, and it is possible in its essence. Its possibility does not require a matter preceding it, for that would lead to its existence being material. Thus it is known that possibility as such does not require matter, and its priority over the temporal existent is only a priority in the mind, which you call essential priority. And that priority is not temporal priority.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents a shubha (sophism) attributed to Ibn Sina and Aristotle, followed by the author's refutation. The shubha argues that every temporal event (hadith) must be preceded by a possibility (imkan) of existence, which is not pure non-existence but a capacity residing in matter. Since matter is only conceivable in time, it follows that the world, if originated, must be preceded by matter and time, leading either to an infinite regress or to a necessary being. This argument, the author notes, led the Mu'tazila to posit that non-existence (al-ma'dum) is a thing. The author's answer begins by redefining the meaning of 'origination from non-existence' (huduth 'an 'adam): it means an existent that has a beginning, but the prior possibility is not a real attribute inhering in an essence that requires matter; rather, it is a mental estimation (taqdir dhihni). Priority and simultaneity are also mental concepts. The author uses the example of the human soul, which is created ex nihilo and has possibility without requiring a pre-existing material substrate. Therefore, possibility as such does not require matter, and its priority over the temporal event is only a priority in the mind (essential priority, sabq dhati), not temporal priority.

تقدير ذهني

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility of existence is a real attribute that must inhere in a pre-existing material substrate.
Correction: Possibility is a mental consideration; it does not require matter, and its priority is mental, not temporal.

Checkpoint
What type of priority does the author say the possibility of a temporal event has over its existence?
A) Temporal priority
B) Essential priority in the mind
C) Causal priority
D) Material priority

Key Takeaway
The refutation shows that possibility is a mental consideration, not a real attribute requiring matter, and its priority is mental, not temporal.

How does this lesson challenge your understanding of how Allah brings things into being from nothing?

Ibn Sina's Objection on Temporal Priority of Possibility
Ibn Sina's objection from necessity of prior possibility and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Sina's argument that every originated thing must be preceded by a possibility of existence in a material substrate, and the consequences of this premise.

Core Idea
Ibn Sina argues that possibility before existence demands a pre-existing matter and time.

Ibn Sina, drawing from Aristotle, presents a sophisticated objection against the Kalam doctrine of creation ex nihilo. He argues that if the world were originated from nothing, it would require an infinite regress of matters and times, or must stop at something that is necessary by another. This objection forced the Mu'tazila to claim that non-existence is a thing. Let us examine the objection step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice how Ibn Sina sets up his premises: every originated thing is preceded by possibility, possibility requires a matter, matter requires time.
Pay attention to the logical chain: originated → possibility → matter → time.
2
Identify the key premises
List the premises: (1) Every originated thing has a prior possibility of existence. (2) Possibility is not pure non-existence but a state requiring a substrate (matter). (3) Matter can only be conceived in time. (4) Therefore, if the world is originated, it is preceded by a temporal possibility in matter.
3
Understand the conclusion
Ibn Sina then gives two options: either this chain regresses infinitely (bāṭil) or it stops at something that has no prior possibility, which would be necessary by another. That is the philosophers' view: the world is eternal but caused.
This conclusion directly challenges the Kalam view of a temporal creation from nothing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة أخرى : قال ابن سينا حكاية عن أرسطاطاليس : كل حادث عن عدم أمر فإنه يسبقه إمكان الوجود ضرورة، وإمكان الوجود ليس هو عدما محضاً، بل هو ما له صلاحية الوجود والعدم، ولن يتصور ذلك إلا في مادة، فكل حادث فإنه يسبقه مادة ثم تلك المادة المتقدمة لا تتصور إلا في زمان ؛ لأن قبل ومع لا يتحقق إلا في زمان والمعدوم قبل هو المعدوم مع ، وليس الإمكان قبل هو الذي يقارن الوجود، فهو إذا متقدم تقدمًا زمانيا، والعالم لو كان حادثا عن عدم لتقدمه إمكان الوجود في مادة تقدما زمانيا ، فهو إما أن يتسلسل فهو باطل، وإما أن يقف على حد لا يسبقه إمكان فلا يسبقه عدم فيكون واجبًا بغيره وهو ما ذهبنا إليه، وهذه الشبهة التي أوقعت المعتزلة في اعتقاد كون المعدوم شيئًا، وعن هذا قصروا الشيئية في الممكن وجوده إلا المستحيل ثبوته.
والجواب : أنا قد بينا أن معنى الحدوث عن عدم أنه هو الموجود الذي له أول لا عن شيء، الإمكان السابق عليه ليس يرجع إلى ذات وهو شيء حتى يحتاج إلى مادة، بل هو أمر راجع إلى التقدير الذهني ؛ لأن ما لا يجوز وجوده لا يتحقق له ثبوت وحدوث والقبلية والمعية راجعة أيضًا إلى التقدير العقلي، وإنما نتصور نحن من حدوث العالم ما يتصورونه من حدوث النفس الإنسانية حادثة لها أول لا عن شيء، حتى يمكن أن يقال : إنها مسبوقة بالعدم ؛ أي: لم تكن فكانت وهي ممكنة الوجود في ذاتها، وإمكانها لا يستدعي مادة تسبقها ، فإن ذلك يؤدي إلى أن يكون وجودها ماديًا، فعلم أن الإمكان من حيث هو إمكان ليس يستدعي مادة وسبقه علي الموجود الحادث ليس إلا سبقا في الذهن سميتموه سبقاً ذاتياً، وذلك السبق ليس سبقا زمانيا.
وكذلك القول في المعلول الأول وساير النفوس فإنها ممكنة الوجود بذواتها، وإمكان وجودها سابق على وجودها سبقاً ذاتيا، وكذلك القول في الجسم الأول الذي هو فلك الأفلاك، ونقول : إن كل حادث حدوثًا زمانيا أو حدوثاً ذاتياً على أصلكم فإنه يسبقه إمكان الوجود، فإن الموجود المحدث قد تردد بين طرفي الوجود والعدم، وهذا التردد والسبق والإمكان كله يرجع إلى تقدير في الذهن، وإلا فالشيء في ذاته على صفة واحدة من الوجود، لكن الوجود باعتبار ذاته انقسم إلى ما يكون وجوده لوجود هو له لذاته ؛ أي هو غير مستفاد له من غيره، فيُقال : الوجود أولى وأول ما يكون وجوده لوجود هو له من غيره فيُقال : الوجود ليس أولى به ولا أول، وهذا الوجود لم يتحقق إلا أن يكون له أول مسبوق بوجود لا أول له ، ويكون له في ذاته إمكان الوجود يعبر عنه بأنه مسبوق بإمكان الوجود، لا أنه وجود يسبقه إمكان الوجود، بل الوجود في ذاته وجود ممكن فقد وجد هاهنا سيقان أحدهما سبق وجود الموجود، والثاني سبق إمكان الوجود.
ولكننا بعدما بحثنا عن السبق الثاني لم نعثر على معنى إلا أن الوجود المستفاد لن يتحقق إلا بأن يكون ممكنا في ذاته مقدرًا فيه تردد بين طرفي الوجود والعدم، واحتاج إلى مرجح لولاه لما حصل له وجود فلو كان كل حادث محتاجا إلى سبق إمكان وكل إمكان محتاجًا إلى مادة وكل مادة إلى زمان تسلسل القول فيه فيُقال : وتلك المادة والزمان يحتاجان إلى مادة وزمان، ولما حصل وجود حادث أصلا فبطل الأصل الذي وضعوا الكلام عليه، بل لا بد من منتهى ينتهي إليه فيكون مبدعًا لا من شيء، ويكون ممكنا في ذاته، ولا يستدعي إمكانه مادة وزمانًا ، فهكذا يجب أن يتصور معنى سبق الإمكان وسبق العدم وسبق الموجد، فإن الموجد يسبق بوجوده من حيث وجوده، ويلزم ذلك أن يسبق العدم والإمكان في الموجد سبقاً تقديريا، وقد تقرر الفرق بين التقدم الذاتي والتقدم الوجودي، فتأمل ذلك.
Another sophism: Ibn Sina, reporting from Aristotle, said: Every originated thing from non-existence is necessarily preceded by the possibility of existence, and the possibility of existence is not pure non-existence, but rather what has the aptitude for existence and non-existence, and that cannot be conceived except in a matter. So every originated thing is preceded by a matter, then that prior matter cannot be conceived except in time, because 'before' and 'with' are only realized in time, and the non-existent 'before' is the non-existent 'with', and the possibility 'before' is not that which accompanies existence, so it is temporally prior. And if the world were originated from non-existence, it would be preceded by the possibility of existence in a matter temporally. Then either it leads to an infinite regress, which is false, or it stops at a limit that is not preceded by possibility, so it is not preceded by non-existence, and thus it is necessary by another, which is what we hold. And this sophism caused the Mu'tazila to believe that the non-existent is a thing, and from this they restricted thingness to possible existence except for the impossible.

The answer: We have already explained that the meaning of origination from non-existence is that it is the existent which has a beginning from nothing, and the prior possibility does not pertain to an essence that is a thing such that it needs a matter, but rather it is a matter pertaining to mental estimation. Because that whose existence is not possible does not have reality and origination, and the 'before' and 'with' also pertain to intellectual estimation. For we only conceive of the origination of the world as we conceive of the origination of the human soul, which is originated having a beginning from nothing, such that it can be said that it is preceded by non-existence, i.e., it was not and then it was, and it is possible in its essence, and its possibility does not require a matter preceding it, because that would lead to its existence being material. Thus it is known that possibility as such does not require a matter, and its priority over the originated existent is only priority in the mind, which you have called essential priority, and that priority is not temporal.

And likewise the statement concerning the first effect and the rest of the souls, for they are possible in their essences, and the possibility of their existence precedes their existence essentially. And likewise the statement concerning the first body, which is the sphere of spheres. And we say: Every originated thing, whether temporal origination or essential origination according to your principle, is preceded by the possibility of existence. For the originated existent has hesitated between the two sides of existence and non-existence, and this hesitation, priority, and possibility all pertain to estimation in the mind. Otherwise, the thing in itself is in one state of existence. But existence considered by itself is divided into what has existence for a being that is for itself, i.e., it is not derived from another, so it is said: existence is more appropriate and first. And what has existence for a being that is from another, so it is said: existence is not more appropriate for it nor first. And this existence is not realized unless it has a beginning preceded by a being that has no beginning, and it has in itself the possibility of existence expressed as being preceded by the possibility of existence, not that it is an existence that is preceded by the possibility of existence. Rather, existence in itself is possible existence. So here there are two priorities: one is the priority of the existence of the existent, and the second is the priority of the possibility of existence.

But after we investigated the second priority, we did not find any meaning except that derived existence is only realized by being possible in itself, with hesitation between the two sides of existence and non-existence, and needing a preponderant without which existence would not be obtained. If every originated thing needed a priority of possibility, and every possibility needed a matter, and every matter needed time, then the statement would lead to infinite regress, and it would be said: that matter and time need matter and time, and no originated existence would ever occur. So the principle upon which they based their discourse is invalid. Rather, there must be a terminal point that ends at something that is created from nothing, and it is possible in itself, and its possibility does not require matter and time. Thus one must conceive the meaning of priority of possibility, priority of non-existence, and priority of the originator. For the originator precedes by His existence in terms of His existence, and it follows that non-existence and possibility in the originated are preceded by a conceptual priority. And the difference between essential priority and existential priority has been established. So consider that.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents an objection (shubha) attributed to Ibn Sina (via Aristotle) and the author's detailed refutation. The objection argues that every originated thing must be preceded by a possibility of existence, which is not pure non-existence but a state requiring a matter (substrate). This matter, in turn, must exist in time. Thus, if the world were originated from nothing, it would require an infinite regress of matters and times, or must stop at something necessary by another (i.e., the world itself as necessarily existent through a cause). This objection led the Mu'tazila to posit that non-existence is a thing (a something). The answer begins by reaffirming that origination from nothing means the thing has a beginning without a prior substrate. The prior possibility is not a real attribute inherent in a subject; it is a mental consideration (taqdīr dhihnī). Similarly, notions of 'before' and 'with' are intellectual, not temporal. Analogy is made to the human soul, which originates from nothing and whose possibility does not require a prior matter. Thus, possibility as such does not demand a matter; its priority over the originated existent is only a priority in the mind, termed 'essential priority' (al-taqaddum al-dhātī), not temporal. The author extends this to the first effect, souls, and the first celestial body. He explains that every originated thing, whether temporally or essentially, is preceded by possibility, but this hesitation between existence and non-existence exists only in mental estimation; in itself, the thing is one. He then distinguishes two types of priority: the priority of the existence of the existent (e.g., the cause) and the priority of possibility. After scrutinizing the second priority, the author concludes that derived existence requires the thing to be possible in itself, needing a preponderant, but this does not entail an actual material substrate preceding it. If every originated thing required such a chain (possibility→matter→time), an infinite regress would occur, invalidating the original principle. Instead, we must reach a terminal point that is created from nothing (mubdaʿ), which is possible in itself without requiring matter or time. Thus, the priority of possibility, non-existence, and the originator are all conceptual, not temporal. The passage concludes by noting that the difference between essential and existential priority is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That possibility of existence is a real attribute inherent in a pre-existing matter, and that priority must be temporal.
Correction: The objection itself presents this as a premise; the author will later refute it. For now, understand that this premise leads to the dilemma.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Sina's objection, what does the possibility of existence require?
A) Pure non-existence
B) A material substrate (matter)
C) Mental estimation
D) An infinite regress

Key Takeaway
Ibn Sina's objection posits that if the world were created from nothing, it would require an infinite regress of matters and times, or else the world must be necessary by another, challenging the Kalam view of temporal creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the possibility of the world's existence required a pre-existing matter, what does that imply about your own dependence on God as the Creator? Do you truly believe in creation ex nihilo, or do you harbor subtle assumptions that something other than God was always there? How would your daily trust in Allah change if you fully internalized that nothing preceded His act of creation?
?
This objection led the Mu'tazila to err about the nature of non-existence. What subtle intellectual assumptions might you be carrying that could lead you away from sound Aqeedah? Are you willing to examine your own beliefs with the same rigor that the Kalam theologians applied to this objection, even if it means abandoning comfortable ideas?
?
The philosophers used this argument to claim the world is necessary by another, stripping it of true contingency. In your heart, do you live as if the world is autonomous, or do you constantly affirm that every moment of its existence is dependent on Allah? What practical steps can you take today to make the reality of creation ex nihilo more than a theological belief—to make it a lived conviction that shapes your gratitude and reliance on Him?

Causality and Created Things

Refutation: Possibility as Mental and Essential Priority
Author's refutation: possibility is mental, priority is essential, no material substrate needed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's refutation that possibility of existence is a mental consideration, not a real attribute, and that its priority over the originated is essential (in the mind), not temporal.

Core Idea
Possibility is a mental construct; its priority is essential, not temporal.

The author responds to Ibn Sina's objection by redefining the nature of origination from non-existence. He argues that the prior possibility is not a real thing inhering in a matter, but a mere mental estimation. He uses the analogy of the human soul, which is originated from nothing and whose possibility does not require a prior matter. The author also distinguishes between two kinds of priority: existential and essential (mental). This refutation defends the Kalam doctrine of creation ex nihilo without falling into infinite regress.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation passage
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note how the author begins by restating the meaning of origination (ḥudūth) as having a beginning from nothing.
The author uses the phrase 'لا عن شيء' (from nothing) to reject the need for a prior matter.
2
Understand the soul analogy
The author compares the origination of the world to the origination of the human soul: it has a beginning from nothing, its possibility does not require a matter.
If the soul were material, its possibility would require matter, but it is not.
3
Learn the two types of priority
The author distinguishes between existential priority (temporal priority of a cause) and essential priority (priority in mental conception). The priority of possibility is essential, not temporal.
This is key to breaking the chain of Ibn Sina's argument.
4
See the refutation of infinite regress
The author argues that if every originated thing required a prior possibility in matter and time, we would have an infinite regress. Instead, we must stop at a thing created from nothing (mubdaʿ) that is possible in itself without matter.
This terminates the regress and supports the Kalam view.

شبهة أخرى : قال ابن سينا حكاية عن أرسطاطاليس : كل حادث عن عدم أمر فإنه يسبقه إمكان الوجود ضرورة، وإمكان الوجود ليس هو عدما محضاً، بل هو ما له صلاحية الوجود والعدم، ولن يتصور ذلك إلا في مادة، فكل حادث فإنه يسبقه مادة ثم تلك المادة المتقدمة لا تتصور إلا في زمان ؛ لأن قبل ومع لا يتحقق إلا في زمان والمعدوم قبل هو المعدوم مع ، وليس الإمكان قبل هو الذي يقارن الوجود، فهو إذا متقدم تقدمًا زمانيا، والعالم لو كان حادثا عن عدم لتقدمه إمكان الوجود في مادة تقدما زمانيا ، فهو إما أن يتسلسل فهو باطل، وإما أن يقف على حد لا يسبقه إمكان فلا يسبقه عدم فيكون واجبًا بغيره وهو ما ذهبنا إليه، وهذه الشبهة التي أوقعت المعتزلة في اعتقاد كون المعدوم شيئًا، وعن هذا قصروا الشيئية في الممكن وجوده إلا المستحيل ثبوته.
والجواب : أنا قد بينا أن معنى الحدوث عن عدم أنه هو الموجود الذي له أول لا عن شيء، الإمكان السابق عليه ليس يرجع إلى ذات وهو شيء حتى يحتاج إلى مادة، بل هو أمر راجع إلى التقدير الذهني ؛ لأن ما لا يجوز وجوده لا يتحقق له ثبوت وحدوث والقبلية والمعية راجعة أيضًا إلى التقدير العقلي، وإنما نتصور نحن من حدوث العالم ما يتصورونه من حدوث النفس الإنسانية حادثة لها أول لا عن شيء، حتى يمكن أن يقال : إنها مسبوقة بالعدم ؛ أي: لم تكن فكانت وهي ممكنة الوجود في ذاتها، وإمكانها لا يستدعي مادة تسبقها ، فإن ذلك يؤدي إلى أن يكون وجودها ماديًا، فعلم أن الإمكان من حيث هو إمكان ليس يستدعي مادة وسبقه علي الموجود الحادث ليس إلا سبقا في الذهن سميتموه سبقاً ذاتياً، وذلك السبق ليس سبقا زمانيا.
وكذلك القول في المعلول الأول وساير النفوس فإنها ممكنة الوجود بذواتها، وإمكان وجودها سابق على وجودها سبقاً ذاتيا، وكذلك القول في الجسم الأول الذي هو فلك الأفلاك، ونقول : إن كل حادث حدوثًا زمانيا أو حدوثاً ذاتياً على أصلكم فإنه يسبقه إمكان الوجود، فإن الموجود المحدث قد تردد بين طرفي الوجود والعدم، وهذا التردد والسبق والإمكان كله يرجع إلى تقدير في الذهن، وإلا فالشيء في ذاته على صفة واحدة من الوجود، لكن الوجود باعتبار ذاته انقسم إلى ما يكون وجوده لوجود هو له لذاته ؛ أي هو غير مستفاد له من غيره، فيُقال : الوجود أولى وأول ما يكون وجوده لوجود هو له من غيره فيُقال : الوجود ليس أولى به ولا أول، وهذا الوجود لم يتحقق إلا أن يكون له أول مسبوق بوجود لا أول له ، ويكون له في ذاته إمكان الوجود يعبر عنه بأنه مسبوق بإمكان الوجود، لا أنه وجود يسبقه إمكان الوجود، بل الوجود في ذاته وجود ممكن فقد وجد هاهنا سيقان أحدهما سبق وجود الموجود، والثاني سبق إمكان الوجود.
ولكننا بعدما بحثنا عن السبق الثاني لم نعثر على معنى إلا أن الوجود المستفاد لن يتحقق إلا بأن يكون ممكنا في ذاته مقدرًا فيه تردد بين طرفي الوجود والعدم، واحتاج إلى مرجح لولاه لما حصل له وجود فلو كان كل حادث محتاجا إلى سبق إمكان وكل إمكان محتاجًا إلى مادة وكل مادة إلى زمان تسلسل القول فيه فيُقال : وتلك المادة والزمان يحتاجان إلى مادة وزمان، ولما حصل وجود حادث أصلا فبطل الأصل الذي وضعوا الكلام عليه، بل لا بد من منتهى ينتهي إليه فيكون مبدعًا لا من شيء، ويكون ممكنا في ذاته، ولا يستدعي إمكانه مادة وزمانًا ، فهكذا يجب أن يتصور معنى سبق الإمكان وسبق العدم وسبق الموجد، فإن الموجد يسبق بوجوده من حيث وجوده، ويلزم ذلك أن يسبق العدم والإمكان في الموجد سبقاً تقديريا، وقد تقرر الفرق بين التقدم الذاتي والتقدم الوجودي، فتأمل ذلك.
Another sophism: Ibn Sina, reporting from Aristotle, said: Every originated thing from non-existence is necessarily preceded by the possibility of existence, and the possibility of existence is not pure non-existence, but rather what has the aptitude for existence and non-existence, and that cannot be conceived except in a matter. So every originated thing is preceded by a matter, then that prior matter cannot be conceived except in time, because 'before' and 'with' are only realized in time, and the non-existent 'before' is the non-existent 'with', and the possibility 'before' is not that which accompanies existence, so it is temporally prior. And if the world were originated from non-existence, it would be preceded by the possibility of existence in a matter temporally. Then either it leads to an infinite regress, which is false, or it stops at a limit that is not preceded by possibility, so it is not preceded by non-existence, and thus it is necessary by another, which is what we hold. And this sophism caused the Mu'tazila to believe that the non-existent is a thing, and from this they restricted thingness to possible existence except for the impossible.

The answer: We have already explained that the meaning of origination from non-existence is that it is the existent which has a beginning from nothing, and the prior possibility does not pertain to an essence that is a thing such that it needs a matter, but rather it is a matter pertaining to mental estimation. Because that whose existence is not possible does not have reality and origination, and the 'before' and 'with' also pertain to intellectual estimation. For we only conceive of the origination of the world as we conceive of the origination of the human soul, which is originated having a beginning from nothing, such that it can be said that it is preceded by non-existence, i.e., it was not and then it was, and it is possible in its essence, and its possibility does not require a matter preceding it, because that would lead to its existence being material. Thus it is known that possibility as such does not require a matter, and its priority over the originated existent is only priority in the mind, which you have called essential priority, and that priority is not temporal.

And likewise the statement concerning the first effect and the rest of the souls, for they are possible in their essences, and the possibility of their existence precedes their existence essentially. And likewise the statement concerning the first body, which is the sphere of spheres. And we say: Every originated thing, whether temporal origination or essential origination according to your principle, is preceded by the possibility of existence. For the originated existent has hesitated between the two sides of existence and non-existence, and this hesitation, priority, and possibility all pertain to estimation in the mind. Otherwise, the thing in itself is in one state of existence. But existence considered by itself is divided into what has existence for a being that is for itself, i.e., it is not derived from another, so it is said: existence is more appropriate and first. And what has existence for a being that is from another, so it is said: existence is not more appropriate for it nor first. And this existence is not realized unless it has a beginning preceded by a being that has no beginning, and it has in itself the possibility of existence expressed as being preceded by the possibility of existence, not that it is an existence that is preceded by the possibility of existence. Rather, existence in itself is possible existence. So here there are two priorities: one is the priority of the existence of the existent, and the second is the priority of the possibility of existence.

But after we investigated the second priority, we did not find any meaning except that derived existence is only realized by being possible in itself, with hesitation between the two sides of existence and non-existence, and needing a preponderant without which existence would not be obtained. If every originated thing needed a priority of possibility, and every possibility needed a matter, and every matter needed time, then the statement would lead to infinite regress, and it would be said: that matter and time need matter and time, and no originated existence would ever occur. So the principle upon which they based their discourse is invalid. Rather, there must be a terminal point that ends at something that is created from nothing, and it is possible in itself, and its possibility does not require matter and time. Thus one must conceive the meaning of priority of possibility, priority of non-existence, and priority of the originator. For the originator precedes by His existence in terms of His existence, and it follows that non-existence and possibility in the originated are preceded by a conceptual priority. And the difference between essential priority and existential priority has been established. So consider that.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage presents an objection (shubha) attributed to Ibn Sina (via Aristotle) and the author's detailed refutation. The objection argues that every originated thing must be preceded by a possibility of existence, which is not pure non-existence but a state requiring a matter (substrate). This matter, in turn, must exist in time. Thus, if the world were originated from nothing, it would require an infinite regress of matters and times, or must stop at something necessary by another (i.e., the world itself as necessarily existent through a cause). This objection led the Mu'tazila to posit that non-existence is a thing (a something). The answer begins by reaffirming that origination from nothing means the thing has a beginning without a prior substrate. The prior possibility is not a real attribute inherent in a subject; it is a mental consideration (taqdīr dhihnī). Similarly, notions of 'before' and 'with' are intellectual, not temporal. Analogy is made to the human soul, which originates from nothing and whose possibility does not require a prior matter. Thus, possibility as such does not demand a matter; its priority over the originated existent is only a priority in the mind, termed 'essential priority' (al-taqaddum al-dhātī), not temporal. The author extends this to the first effect, souls, and the first celestial body. He explains that every originated thing, whether temporally or essentially, is preceded by possibility, but this hesitation between existence and non-existence exists only in mental estimation; in itself, the thing is one. He then distinguishes two types of priority: the priority of the existence of the existent (e.g., the cause) and the priority of possibility. After scrutinizing the second priority, the author concludes that derived existence requires the thing to be possible in itself, needing a preponderant, but this does not entail an actual material substrate preceding it. If every originated thing required such a chain (possibility→matter→time), an infinite regress would occur, invalidating the original principle. Instead, we must reach a terminal point that is created from nothing (mubdaʿ), which is possible in itself without requiring matter or time. Thus, the priority of possibility, non-existence, and the originator are all conceptual, not temporal. The passage concludes by noting that the difference between essential and existential priority is established.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That possibility of existence is a real attribute inhering in a material substrate, and that its priority must be temporal.
Correction: The author argues that possibility is a mental consideration and its priority is essential (in the mind), not temporal.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the nature of the priority of possibility (sabq al-imkān) over an originated thing?
A) It is a temporal priority in a material substrate.
B) It is a priority in mental estimation only, not real or temporal.
C) It is a relational attribute inherent in non-existence.
D) It is a necessary condition for the infinite regress of matter.

Key Takeaway
The refutation shows that creation from nothing does not entail a material substrate; possibility is a mental consideration, and its priority is essential, not temporal, thus avoiding infinite regress.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your own existence, do you ever catch yourself assuming there must be a material cause for everything? How does the author's argument that 'possibility is mental' challenge you to rethink your dependence on physical explanations?
?
The author says that the priority of possibility is only in the mind, not in time. Is it possible that you are confusing your mental categories (like 'before' and 'after') with actual reality? How does this affect your understanding of God's act of creation?
?
If the first originated thing was created from nothing without any prior matter or time, what does that imply about your own reliance on secondary causes? Are you willing to trust that God can bring about existence directly, without any intermediate chain, even in your daily life?

The Priority of Possibility over Existence
The author states the essential priority of possibility over existence for originated beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that possibility is essentially prior to existence for all originated things.

Core Idea
Possibility precedes existence by essence, not by time.

The author begins by establishing a foundational principle: every originated thing is possible in itself, and its possibility of existing precedes its actual existence. This is not a temporal priority but an essential one. He applies this to the first effect, souls, and the first body, then generalizes the rule.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the use of terms like 'possible in itself' and 'essential precedence'.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the entities mentioned
The author mentions the first effect, souls, and the first body. These are examples of originated things that are possible in themselves.
These are key concepts in kalam cosmology.
3
Understand the general principle
The author states that every originated thing, whether temporal or essential, is preceded by possibility. This is the core idea.
4
Reflect on the meaning of essential precedence
Essential precedence means that possibility is logically prior, not temporally. The thing's nature requires possibility before existence.
This distinguishes kalam from philosophical views.

وكذلك القول في المعلول الأول وساير النفوس فإنها ممكنة الوجود بذواتها، وإمكان وجودها سابق على وجودها سبقاً ذاتيا، وكذلك القول في الجسم الأول الذي هو فلك الأفلاك، ونقول : إن كل حادث حدوثًا زمانيا أو حدوثاً ذاتياً على أصلكم فإنه يسبقه إمكان الوجود، فإن الموجود المحدث قد تردد بين طرفي الوجود والعدم، وهذا التردد والسبق والإمكان كله يرجع إلى تقدير في الذهن، وإلا فالشيء في ذاته على صفة واحدة من الوجود، لكن الوجود باعتبار ذاته انقسم إلى ما يكون وجوده لوجود هو له لذاته ؛ أي هو غير مستفاد له من غيره، فيُقال : الوجود أولى وأول ما يكون وجوده لوجود هو له من غيره فيُقال : الوجود ليس أولى به ولا أول، وهذا الوجود لم يتحقق إلا أن يكون له أول مسبوق بوجود لا أول له ، ويكون له في ذاته إمكان الوجود يعبر عنه بأنه مسبوق بإمكان الوجود، لا أنه وجود يسبقه إمكان الوجود، بل الوجود في ذاته وجود ممكن فقد وجد هاهنا سيقان أحدهما سبق وجود الموجود، والثاني سبق إمكان الوجود. ولكننا بعدما بحثنا عن السبق الثاني لم نعثر على معنى إلا أن الوجود المستفاد لن يتحقق إلا بأن يكون ممكنا في ذاته مقدرًا فيه تردد بين طرفي الوجود والعدم، واحتاج إلى مرجح لولاه لما حصل له وجود فلو كان كل حادث محتاجا إلى سبق إمكان وكل إمكان محتاجًا إلى مادة وكل مادة إلى زمان تسلسل القول فيه فيُقال : وتلك المادة والزمان يحتاجان إلى مادة وزمان، ولما حصل وجود حادث أصلا فبطل الأصل الذي وضعوا الكلام عليه، بل لا بد من منتهى ينتهي إليه فيكون مبدعًا لا من شيء، ويكون ممكنا في ذاته، ولا يستدعي إمكانه مادة وزمانًا ، فهكذا يجب أن يتصور معنى سبق الإمكان وسبق العدم وسبق الموجد، فإن الموجد يسبق بوجوده من حيث وجوده، ويلزم ذلك أن يسبق العدم والإمكان في الموجد سبقاً تقديريا، وقد تقرر الفرق بين التقدم الذاتي والتقدم الوجودي، فتأمل ذلك.
And likewise the statement concerning the first effect and the rest of the souls: they are possible in existence by themselves, and their possibility of existence precedes their existence by an essential precedence. And likewise the statement concerning the first body, which is the sphere of spheres. And we say: Every occurrence, whether temporal occurrence or essential occurrence according to your principle, is preceded by the possibility of existence. For the originated existent has been undecided between the two extremes of existence and non-existence. And this undecidedness, precedence, and possibility all refer back to an estimation in the mind; otherwise the thing in itself is upon a single attribute of existence. But existence, with respect to itself, is divided into that whose existence is for an existence that belongs to it in itself—i.e., it is not acquired from another—so it is said: existence is more appropriate. And the first thing whose existence is for an existence that belongs to it from another is said: existence is not more appropriate for it, nor is it first. And this existence is not realized unless it has a first preceded by an existence that has no first, and it has in itself a possibility of existence expressed by its being preceded by the possibility of existence, not that it is an existence that is preceded by the possibility of existence. Rather, existence in itself is a possible existence. So here two successions have occurred: one is the precedence of the existence of the existent, and the second is the precedence of the possibility of existence. But after we investigated the second precedence, we did not find any meaning except that acquired existence is not realized unless it is possible in itself, estimated with an undecidedness between the two extremes of existence and non-existence, and it needs a preponderant without which existence would not occur for it. For if every temporal event needed a precedence of possibility, and every possibility needed matter, and every matter needed time, then the discourse would regress infinitely, so it would be said: that matter and time need matter and time. And no temporal existence would occur at all, so the principle upon which they based their discourse is invalidated. Rather, there must be a final term at which it ends, such that it creates from nothing, and is possible in itself, and its possibility does not require matter and time. Thus the meaning of precedence of possibility, precedence of non-existence, and precedence of the causative agent must be conceived: for the causative agent precedes by its existence by virtue of its existence, and it follows from that that non-existence and possibility precede in the causative agent by a notional precedence. And the difference between essential priority and existential priority has been established, so reflect on that.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the nature of possibility and existence, and a refutation of infinite regress in the chain of causes. The author begins by discussing the first effect and souls: they are possible in themselves, and their possibility precedes their existence essentially. Similarly for the first body (the outermost sphere). He then states a general principle: every originated thing, whether temporally or essentially originated, is preceded by the possibility of existence. The originated existent wavers between existence and non-existence; this wavering, precedence, and possibility are all mental estimations—the thing itself has a single state regarding existence. Existence, considered in itself, is divided into what exists by itself (necessary, not acquired) and what exists from another (possible). The latter requires a first that is preceded by an existence that has no first (the Necessary Existent). The possible existent is described as being preceded by possibility, not as an existence that is preceded by possibility; rather, its existence is possible. Then the author clarifies that two types of precedence occur: precedence of the existence of the existent (the cause precedes the effect) and precedence of the possibility of existence (the possibility is prior to the actual existence). Investigating the second precedence, he concludes that acquired existence must be possible in itself, with an estimated wavering, and it needs a preponderant. He then refutes the view (likely of the philosophers) that every contingent needs a preceding possibility, each possibility needs matter, and each matter needs time, leading to an infinite regress—which would prevent any originated existence. Instead, there must be an endpoint: a creator who creates from nothing, is possible in Himself, and His possibility does not require matter or time. Finally, he summarizes the meanings of precedence (of possibility, non-existence, and the causative agent) and distinguishes between essential priority and existential priority, urging the reader to reflect.

intermediate

Mental Estimation and Refutation of Infinite Regress
Explains possibility as mental estimation and refutes infinite regress in matter and time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that possibility is a mental estimation and that the chain of possibility, matter, and time cannot regress infinitely.

Core Idea
Possibility is an estimated wavering in the mind, and infinite regress of causes is impossible.

The author deepens the analysis: the 'wavering' between existence and non-existence is a mental estimation, not a real attribute. He then presents the view that every temporal event needs a preceding possibility, which needs matter, which needs time, leading to an infinite regress. This regress invalidates the original argument, so there must be a different account.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning of this lesson's selection. Notice the key phrases 'تردد' (wavering) and 'تقدير في الذهن' (estimation in the mind).
2
Understand the mental nature of possibility
The author clarifies that the undecidedness, precedence, and possibility are all mental estimations, not real attributes of the thing itself. The thing in itself has a single state of existence.
This is a crucial distinction.
3
Identify the two successions
The author mentions two types of precedence: precedence of the existence of the existent (cause precedes effect) and precedence of the possibility of existence (possibility precedes actual existence).
4
Grasp the refutation of infinite regress
The author argues that if every temporal event required a preceding possibility, which required matter, which required time, this would go on infinitely, preventing any existence. Therefore, the original premise is invalid.

وكذلك القول في المعلول الأول وساير النفوس فإنها ممكنة الوجود بذواتها، وإمكان وجودها سابق على وجودها سبقاً ذاتيا، وكذلك القول في الجسم الأول الذي هو فلك الأفلاك، ونقول : إن كل حادث حدوثًا زمانيا أو حدوثاً ذاتياً على أصلكم فإنه يسبقه إمكان الوجود، فإن الموجود المحدث قد تردد بين طرفي الوجود والعدم، وهذا التردد والسبق والإمكان كله يرجع إلى تقدير في الذهن، وإلا فالشيء في ذاته على صفة واحدة من الوجود، لكن الوجود باعتبار ذاته انقسم إلى ما يكون وجوده لوجود هو له لذاته ؛ أي هو غير مستفاد له من غيره، فيُقال : الوجود أولى وأول ما يكون وجوده لوجود هو له من غيره فيُقال : الوجود ليس أولى به ولا أول، وهذا الوجود لم يتحقق إلا أن يكون له أول مسبوق بوجود لا أول له ، ويكون له في ذاته إمكان الوجود يعبر عنه بأنه مسبوق بإمكان الوجود، لا أنه وجود يسبقه إمكان الوجود، بل الوجود في ذاته وجود ممكن فقد وجد هاهنا سيقان أحدهما سبق وجود الموجود، والثاني سبق إمكان الوجود. ولكننا بعدما بحثنا عن السبق الثاني لم نعثر على معنى إلا أن الوجود المستفاد لن يتحقق إلا بأن يكون ممكنا في ذاته مقدرًا فيه تردد بين طرفي الوجود والعدم، واحتاج إلى مرجح لولاه لما حصل له وجود فلو كان كل حادث محتاجا إلى سبق إمكان وكل إمكان محتاجًا إلى مادة وكل مادة إلى زمان تسلسل القول فيه فيُقال : وتلك المادة والزمان يحتاجان إلى مادة وزمان، ولما حصل وجود حادث أصلا فبطل الأصل الذي وضعوا الكلام عليه، بل لا بد من منتهى ينتهي إليه فيكون مبدعًا لا من شيء، ويكون ممكنا في ذاته، ولا يستدعي إمكانه مادة وزمانًا ، فهكذا يجب أن يتصور معنى سبق الإمكان وسبق العدم وسبق الموجد، فإن الموجد يسبق بوجوده من حيث وجوده، ويلزم ذلك أن يسبق العدم والإمكان في الموجد سبقاً تقديريا، وقد تقرر الفرق بين التقدم الذاتي والتقدم الوجودي، فتأمل ذلك.
And likewise the statement concerning the first effect and the rest of the souls: they are possible in existence by themselves, and their possibility of existence precedes their existence by an essential precedence. And likewise the statement concerning the first body, which is the sphere of spheres. And we say: Every occurrence, whether temporal occurrence or essential occurrence according to your principle, is preceded by the possibility of existence. For the originated existent has been undecided between the two extremes of existence and non-existence. And this undecidedness, precedence, and possibility all refer back to an estimation in the mind; otherwise the thing in itself is upon a single attribute of existence. But existence, with respect to itself, is divided into that whose existence is for an existence that belongs to it in itself—i.e., it is not acquired from another—so it is said: existence is more appropriate. And the first thing whose existence is for an existence that belongs to it from another is said: existence is not more appropriate for it, nor is it first. And this existence is not realized unless it has a first preceded by an existence that has no first, and it has in itself a possibility of existence expressed by its being preceded by the possibility of existence, not that it is an existence that is preceded by the possibility of existence. Rather, existence in itself is a possible existence. So here two successions have occurred: one is the precedence of the existence of the existent, and the second is the precedence of the possibility of existence. But after we investigated the second precedence, we did not find any meaning except that acquired existence is not realized unless it is possible in itself, estimated with an undecidedness between the two extremes of existence and non-existence, and it needs a preponderant without which existence would not occur for it. For if every temporal event needed a precedence of possibility, and every possibility needed matter, and every matter needed time, then the discourse would regress infinitely, so it would be said: that matter and time need matter and time. And no temporal existence would occur at all, so the principle upon which they based their discourse is invalidated. Rather, there must be a final term at which it ends, such that it creates from nothing, and is possible in itself, and its possibility does not require matter and time. Thus the meaning of precedence of possibility, precedence of non-existence, and precedence of the causative agent must be conceived: for the causative agent precedes by its existence by virtue of its existence, and it follows from that that non-existence and possibility precede in the causative agent by a notional precedence. And the difference between essential priority and existential priority has been established, so reflect on that.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is an argument about the nature of possibility and existence, and a refutation of infinite regress in the chain of causes. The author begins by discussing the first effect and souls: they are possible in themselves, and their possibility precedes their existence essentially. Similarly for the first body (the outermost sphere). He then states a general principle: every originated thing, whether temporally or essentially originated, is preceded by the possibility of existence. The originated existent wavers between existence and non-existence; this wavering, precedence, and possibility are all mental estimations—the thing itself has a single state regarding existence. Existence, considered in itself, is divided into what exists by itself (necessary, not acquired) and what exists from another (possible). The latter requires a first that is preceded by an existence that has no first (the Necessary Existent). The possible existent is described as being preceded by possibility, not as an existence that is preceded by possibility; rather, its existence is possible. Then the author clarifies that two types of precedence occur: precedence of the existence of the existent (the cause precedes the effect) and precedence of the possibility of existence (the possibility is prior to the actual existence). Investigating the second precedence, he concludes that acquired existence must be possible in itself, with an estimated wavering, and it needs a preponderant. He then refutes the view (likely of the philosophers) that every contingent needs a preceding possibility, each possibility needs matter, and each matter needs time, leading to an infinite regress—which would prevent any originated existence. Instead, there must be an endpoint: a creator who creates from nothing, is possible in Himself, and His possibility does not require matter or time. Finally, he summarizes the meanings of precedence (of possibility, non-existence, and the causative agent) and distinguishes between essential priority and existential priority, urging the reader to reflect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Possibility is a real attribute that exists temporally before the thing.
Correction: Possibility is a mental estimation; the thing itself has only one state of existence.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what happens if every temporal event requires a preceding possibility, which requires matter, which requires time?
A) The chain ends with matter
B) The chain ends with time
C) The chain regresses infinitely and no existence occurs
D) The chain is accepted as it is

Key Takeaway
Possibility is an estimated mental concept, and infinite regress in causes is impossible because it prevents any existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your existence and everything you rely on ultimately depend on a First Cause that is not itself caused, or do you live as if the chain of causes goes on forever? How would your sense of security change if you fully internalized that all secondary causes are dependent on Him?
?
When you face uncertainty or indecision, do you seek the Preponderant who alone can tip the balance, or do you remain trapped in the mental estimation of possibilities as if they were real? What would it mean to turn to Him in your moments of wavering?
?
If infinite regress is impossible, then there is an ultimate stop. Are you living as if there is an ultimate purpose and end to your life, or are you caught in an endless pursuit of worldly causes that never satisfy?

The Creator and the Distinction Between Priority Types
Concludes that a creator is necessary and distinguishes between essential and existential priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that there must be a creator whose possibility does not require matter or time, and that essential and existential priority are different.

Core Idea
The creator is possible in Himself but needs no matter or time, breaking the regress.

After refuting the infinite regress, the author concludes that there must be an endpoint: a creator who creates from nothing. This creator is possible in Himself, but His possibility does not require matter or time. The author then distinguishes between essential priority (logical) and existential priority (temporal or causal).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the final part of the source passage. Notice the claim that there must be a final term (منتهى) that creates from nothing.
2
Understand the creator's attributes
The creator is 'possible in Himself' but His possibility does not require matter or time. This is a unique status.
This resolves the regress.
3
Grasp the three types of precedence
The author mentions precedence of possibility, precedence of non-existence, and precedence of the causative agent. The causative agent precedes by his existence.
4
Distinguish essential vs existential priority
The author refers to the difference between essential priority (logical) and existential priority (real causal priority). Both are valid in different senses.
Reflect on this distinction.

Ibn Sina's Doubt and the Three-Premise Response
Presents Ibn Sina's doubt about the world's preponderant and refutes it by requiring three premises.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Sina's argument that a possible world requires a preponderant, and how the response refutes it by demanding three premises.

Core Idea
Ibn Sina's doubt collapses unless three key premises are proven.

This passage presents one of the most famous theological doubts—attributed to Ibn Sina—concerning the creation of the world. He argues that if the world is only possible in itself, its existence requires a preponderant, but if that preponderant is eternal and unchanging, how can a temporal effect arise? The response does not directly answer but instead demands that the objector prove three premises first. This sets up the framework for a detailed refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Ibn Sina's doubt is presented as a logical dilemma.
2
Identify the structure of the doubt
The doubt has two main parts: (a) the need for a preponderant, (b) a reductio ad absurdum showing that assuming inactivity leads to contradiction. Find these parts.
The reductio is: if the essence is the same and no action occurred before, then no action should occur now.
3
Understand the three-premise response
The response lists three premises that the doubter must prove before the doubt can stand. Write them down in order. Then notice how the text begins to tackle the first premise.
The first premise is about pre-eternity. The passage mentions two aspects, but the details are cut off.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شبهة أخرى اعتمد عليها أبو علي بن سينا قال أسلم أن العالم بما فيه من الجواهر والأعراض جايز الوجود لذاته، لكن كلامنا في أنه هل هو واجب الوجود بغيره دايم الوجود بدوامه؟ قال : والجايز أن لا يوجد وأن يوجد، وإذا تخصص بالوجود احتاج إلى مرجح الجانب الوجود، والحال لا يخلو إما أن يُقال : ما يجوز أن يوجد عن المرجح يجب أن يوجد حتى لا يتراخى عنه، وإما أن يُقال: لا يجب أن يوجد حتى يتراخى عنه ، ثم يوجد بعد أن لم يوجد، لكن العقل الصريح الذي لم يكذب يقضي أن الذات الواحدة إذا كانت من جميع جهاتها واحدة وهي كانت وكان لا يوجد عنها شيء فيما قبل مع جواز أن يوجد الآن كذلك ، فالآن لا يوجد عنها شيء وإذا كان قد وجد فقد حدث أمر لا محالة قصد عن وإرادة وطبع ،وقدرة، أو تمكن وغرض، أو سبب من الأسباب، ثم لا يخلو ذلك السبب إما أن يحدث في ذاته صفة، أو يحدث أمرًا مباينا عنه، والكلام في ذلك الحادث على أي وجه كان كالكلام في العالم، فإذا لا يجوز أن يحدث أمر ما، وإذا لم يجز فلا فرق بين حال أن يفعل وبين حال أن لا يفعل وقد وجد الفعل فهو خلف، وإنما لزمنا هذا لأنا وضعنا في التقدير العقلي ذاتا معطلة عن الفعل، وهو باطل فنقيضه حق. والجواب :قلنا : أنتم مطالبون بإثبات ثلاث مقدمات : إحداها : إثبات جواز وجود العالم في الأزل. والثانية : إثبات أن ما يجوز وجوده يجب وجوده. والثالثة إثبات سبب حادث لأمر حادث. أما الأولى فنحن قد بينا استحالة وجود أمر جايز في ذاته مع وجود موجود واجب في ذاته في الأزل من وجهين :
Another doubt relied upon by Abu Ali Ibn Sina. He said: I concede that the world, including its substances and accidents, is possible in existence by itself, but our discussion is about whether it is necessary in existence through another, enduring in existence through His endurance. He said: The possible is that it may not exist and may exist. And when it is specified with existence, it needs a preponderant for the side of existence. And the situation is inevitably either that it is said: what is possible to exist from the preponderant must exist so that it is not deferred from it, or that it is said: it is not necessary for it to exist until it is deferred from it, then it exists after it did not exist. But sound reason that does not lie judges that one essence, when it is one in all its aspects, and it was and nothing existed from it before, while it is possible to exist now likewise, then now nothing exists from it. And if it has existed, then an occurrence has inevitably occurred: intent and will, nature and power, or ability and purpose, or some cause among causes. Then that cause is either that it occurs in itself as an attribute, or it occurs as something separate from it. And the discourse concerning that occurrence, in whatever manner it is, is like the discourse concerning the world. So if it is not permissible for an occurrence to occur, and if it is not permissible, then there is no difference between the state of acting and the state of not acting, and action has occurred, so it is a contradiction. And we are forced into this because we assumed in the mental estimation an essence that is inactive of action, and that is invalid, so its opposite is true. The answer: We said: You are required to prove three premises: The first: proving the permissibility of the world's existence in pre-eternity. The second: proving that what is possible to exist must exist. The third: proving an originated cause for an originated matter. As for the first, we have already shown the impossibility of a thing possible in itself existing along with an existent necessary in itself in pre-eternity from two aspects:
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage presents an objection (شبهة) from Ibn Sina and the beginning of the response. The objection: Ibn Sina concedes the world is possible in itself, but asks whether it is necessary through another and eternal through God's eternity. For a possible being, when it becomes specified with existence, it needs a preponderant. Then either that possible must exist immediately from the preponderant (no delay) or it may be delayed. Sound reason says: if a single essence remains the same in all respects and previously produced nothing, and it is possible to produce now, then now also nothing should occur. But if it did produce, then some new cause must have arisen—either an attribute in itself or an external cause—and that cause is itself a new event, leading to the same problem (infinite regress). Thus, if no new event can occur, there is no difference between acting and not acting, yet action occurred, contradiction. This contradiction arises only because we assumed the essence to be inactive in a mental estimation, so that assumption is false, and its opposite (that it can act without change) is true. The response: The author (al-Shahrastani?) replies that the opponent must prove three premises: (1) the world's existence is possible in pre-eternity, (2) what is possible to exist must exist (i.e., the preponderant necessitates immediate existence), and (3) there must be an originated cause for an originated matter. Then he begins discussing the first premise, stating they have already shown the impossibility of a possible existing alongside the Necessary in pre-eternity from two aspects (but the text cuts off).

Key Terms
شبهة
مرجح
جايز الوجود
واجب الوجود بغيره
مقدمات
أزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Ibn Sina's doubt proves that the world cannot be created at all, or that it must be eternal.
Correction: The response shows that the doubt depends on unproven premises about the necessity of immediate causation and the impossibility of temporal origination. It does not disprove creation; it only reveals assumptions that need justification.

Checkpoint
What is the third premise that the opponent must prove according to the response?
A) The world's existence is possible in pre-eternity
B) What is possible to exist must exist
C) An originated cause for an originated matter
D) The preponderant must act immediately

Key Takeaway
Ibn Sina's logical doubt is neutralized by showing it depends on unestablished premises about pre-eternity, necessity, and causality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a doubt that seems to challenge your faith, do you examine its hidden assumptions or let it shake your certainty? Which premise in your belief about God's power might you be holding without proof?
?
Ibn Sina's doubt assumes that an unchanging God cannot initiate new actions. Do you ever live as if God's power is limited by your own understanding of cause and effect? Have you stopped asking for something because you deemed it impossible?
?
The response demands proving three premises before the doubt can stand. Are there truths of your faith that you accept without ever trying to understand their logical foundation? What would change if you sought that understanding rather than relying on inherited belief?

intermediate
5 min
Possibility Negates Eternal Necessity
Sanusi refutes the opponent's claim about possible things.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why acknowledging that something is possible of existence means it cannot be eternal and requires a cause to bring it into existence.

Core Idea
Possibility in one aspect implies possibility in all aspects.

This passage tackles a key objection: if the world is possible, why can't it be eternal? The opponent claims possibility still allows eternal existence. Sanusi shows that this is self-contradictory and explains why possibility destroys any claim to necessity or perpetuity.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's statement
Read the first part of the Arabic carefully: 'العالم جايز الوجود وكل جايز وجوده يجب وجوده أزلا وأبدًا'. Notice the claim that possible things must exist forever.
This is the view Sanusi is refuting.
2
Identify the contradiction
Sanusi says this combines two contradictory propositions. Reflect on why 'possible' and 'must exist forever' cannot both be true.
Hint: possibility allows for non-existence.
3
Trace the implication of possibility
The passage argues that if possibility enters from one aspect, it enters from all – time, quantity, form. Think about why possibility cannot be restricted to one dimension.
This is the core logical move.
4
Understand the need for a specifying agent
When a possible thing is specified with one of two alternatives, it needs a cause (مخصص) to choose. This negates any necessity or perpetuity.
This concludes the refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقولكم : العالم جايز الوجود وكل جايز وجوده يجب وجوده أزلا وأبدًا جمع بين قضيتين متناقضتين، ومن اعترف بالجواز والإمكان فقد سلم المسألة من كل وجه، فإن الشيء إذا تطرق إليه الجواز في الوجود من وجه تطرق إليه الجواز من ساير الوجوه؛ أعني : الوقت والمقدار والشكل، إذا كان الموجود قابلا لها أو لواحد منها، والداير بين وجوه الجواز إذا تخصص بأحد الجايزين دون الثاني احتاج إلى مخصص وانتفى الوجوب والدوام عنه.
And your statement: 'The world is possible of existence, and everything possible of existence must exist eternally and perpetually' combines two contradictory propositions. Whoever acknowledges contingency and possibility has conceded the matter entirely, for if possibility in existence enters into a thing from one aspect, it enters into it from all aspects; I mean: time, quantity, and form, if the existent is receptive to them or to one of them. And that which is subject to alternative possibilities, when it is specified with one of the two possibles to the exclusion of the other, it needs a specifying agent, and necessity and perpetuity are negated from it.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage refutes an opponent's claim that possible existents must exist eternally. The author argues that acknowledging possibility in any aspect implies possibility in all aspects, including time, quantity, form. If something is possible, it can be or not be, so it cannot be necessary. Thus, it needs a specifying agent (مخصص) to tip the balance, negating necessity and perpetuity.

Key Terms
جواز
إمكان
مخصص
وجوب
دوام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Opponent thinks that 'possible of existence' does not contradict eternal existence; that a thing can be possible and yet necessarily exist forever.
Correction: Possibility inherently allows non-existence, so it cannot entail necessity or perpetuity. Possibility in one aspect entails possibility in all aspects, requiring a cause for specification and negating eternity.

Checkpoint
What does the author say is needed when a possible thing is specified with one of two possibles?
A) A specifying agent (مخصص)
B) Time
C) Necessity
D) Another possible

Key Takeaway
Possibility in any aspect entails possibility in all aspects, so a possible thing cannot be eternal and requires a specifying agent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You believe that every detail of your existence—your time, your form, your very being—is contingent and specified by God. But do you truly live with that awareness? When you make plans or worry about the future, are you not acting as if things are necessary or under your control? What would change in your daily habits if you fully internalized that only God is necessary and you depend on His specification every moment? Resolve to start each day with a conscious acknowledgment of your contingency (e.g., saying 'There is no power and no strength except with God').
?
This lesson shows that possibility in one aspect implies possibility in all aspects. Consider an area of your life where you accept uncertainty (e.g., your career) but demand certainty in another (e.g., your health or relationships). How is that contradictory? Where do you need to submit to the fact that nothing in this world is necessary except God? Think of one specific worry you can surrender to Him today, acknowledging that it is possible and only He can specify it for good.
?
Sanusi argues that a possible thing requires a specifying agent. Have you ever pondered that your very existence at this moment, in this form, in this time and place, is not a coincidence but a choice by the Creator? How does that realization make you feel—does it fill you with gratitude, accountability, or both? What is one way you can respond to that specification today, such as a specific act of worship or service that honors the One who specified you here and now?

Second Proof: Impossibility of Infinite Events
Presents the second proof against eternality using infinite events and answers an objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second proof against the world's eternality: that an infinite series of past events is impossible.

Core Idea
An infinite number of past events is impossible, so the world cannot be eternal.

The proof against the world being eternal that we have already seen is based on possibility and a specifying agent. The second proof is simpler: if the world were eternal, there would have been an infinite number of past events. But we have already demonstrated that an infinite series of temporal events is impossible. This short passage presents that argument and answers a natural objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a statement of the proof, then an objection and its answer.
2
Identify the logical steps
Identify the premise (infinite events are impossible) and the conclusion (the world cannot be eternal). Then find the objection and the answer.
The answer simply refers back to the premise.
3
Compare with the first proof
Consider how this proof differs from the earlier argument based on contingency and a specifying agent. Both lead to the same conclusion.
This proof is more direct and does not rely on the concept of a specifying agent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الوجه الثاني في بيان الاستحالة أن الحوادث التي لا تتناهى قد تبين استحالتها. فإن قيل : ما المانع من وجود العالم في الأزل؟ كان الجواب استحالة حوادث لا تتناهى لما بينا من البرهان الدال عليه.
As for the second aspect in demonstrating impossibility: that events which are infinite have been shown to be impossible. So if it is said: What prevents the world from existing in eternity? The answer is: the impossibility of infinite events, according to what we have demonstrated of the proof indicating that.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This is a concise proof and objection-answer. The proof is that infinite temporal events are impossible; hence the world cannot be eternal because that would entail an infinite number of past events. The objection asking why the world cannot be eternal is answered by reference to this proof.

Key Terms

لا تتناهى
استحالة

Checkpoint

A) The necessity of the Necessary Being

C) The possibility of the world
D) The specifying agent

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of infinite temporal events directly refutes the possibility of an eternal world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If an infinite number of past events is impossible, then your own life is part of a finite sequence. How does the certainty that the world had a beginning affect your sense of urgency about your purpose in this limited span?
?
The objection 'What prevents the world from existing in eternity?' may cross your own mind when you consider the vastness of time. Have you ever used the idea of an eternal universe to avoid the personal implications of a Creator? What would it mean for you to accept that the world is not eternal?
?
The proof rests on the impossibility of infinite events. Do you truly live as if your deeds are finite and accountable? How would your next 24 hours change if you deeply believed that time is not endless?

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
