The Contradiction if Contingent Were Necessary
Proof of contradiction if contingent beings became necessary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical contradiction that would arise if every possible being became necessary, specifically that the infinite would have to exist all at once, contradicting the observed order and finitude of existence.

Core Idea
If every possible thing were necessary, the infinite would exist all at once—but reality shows order and limitation.

This passage presents a powerful argument by contradiction. The author begins by noting that the possible (al-ja'iz) is infinite in number. If each possible became necessary, all would have to exist simultaneously. Yet the world we observe is finite and ordered, with things occurring in sequence. The contradiction proves that the original assumption is false, and the argument points to a deeper distinction in types of priority and posteriority.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage slowly, then the English translation. Notice the logical flow: assumption, consequence, observation, contradiction.
The passage uses technical terms like al-ja'iz and al-wajib.
2
Identify the key terms
Find the terms 'الجائز' (possible), 'الواجب' (necessary), 'التناقض' (contradiction), 'الترتيب' (order). Understand their roles in the argument.
3
Trace the contradiction
Follow the argument: possibility is infinite → if necessary, infinite exists at once → but actual existence shows order and finitude → contradiction.
The author also mentions a condition of order in essences and existents.
4
Connect to the broader context
The passage builds on a prior discussion of types of priority and posteriority. Consider why this distinction is needed to resolve the contradiction.
This is a typical kalam proof for the existence of a necessary being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما التناقض من حيث المعنى فهو أن الجايز وجوده مما لا يتناهى، فلو كان ما جاز وجوده وجب وجوده لوجد ما لا يتناهى دفعة واحدة وإذا شرط الترتيب في الذوات حتى حصل في الوجود أول ثم ثان ثم ثالث، ثم ينتهي إلى موجودات محصورة، كذلك يشترط [؟] الترتيب في الموجود حتى حصل موجود (۳) له أول ثم ثان ثم ثالث، فالترتيب في الذوات تقدمًا وتأخرًا كالترتيب في الموجودات أولا وآخرا، وهذا بناء على ما ذكرناه من إثبات قسم آخر في أقسام التقدم والتأخر، وذلك واجب الرعاية.
As for the contradiction from the perspective of meaning: it is that that whose existence is possible is among that which is infinite. So if what is possible in existence were necessary in existence, then what is infinite would exist all at once. And if order is conditioned in essences so that existence occurs first, then second, then third, then it ends at limited existents, similarly order is conditioned [؟] in existence so that an existent occurs that has a first, then a second, then a third. So the order in essences as priority and posteriority is like the order in existents as first and last. And this is based on what we have mentioned regarding the establishment of another division among the divisions of priority and posteriority, and that must be observed.
Source pages p. 37

Commentary
This passage is a proof of contradiction. It begins by stating that the possible (al-ja'iz) is infinite in the sense that there is no limit to what can possibly exist. If each possible were to become necessary (wajib), then all possible things would have to exist simultaneously, which is impossible because we observe that the actual world contains only a finite set of existents arranged in an order (first, second, third). The author argues that if we require order in the essences (al-dhat) themselves for them to appear in existence sequentially, then similarly we must require order in the existents (al-mawjudat) that actually come to be. Consequently, the resulting existents are limited and ordered, contradicting the initial assumption of infinite simultaneous existence. The conclusion is that the original supposition (that contingent things could become necessary) is false, and this argument highlights the need for a different kind of priority and posteriority—perhaps essential or causal priority—to resolve the contradiction. The author reminds the reader that this argument builds on an earlier distinction of another division among types of priority and posteriority.

Key Terms
الجائز
الواجب
التناقض
الترتيب
التقدم
التأخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the infinite here means temporal infinity (endless time).
Correction: It actually refers to the multitude of possible beings – there is no limit to what can possibly exist, regardless of time.

Checkpoint
What is the main contradiction that arises if every possible being were to become necessary?
A) They would all exist at once, but order implies finitude.
B) They would none exist because necessity contradicts possibility.
C) They would exist in a random order without cause.
D) They would become eternal and uncreated.

Key Takeaway
The assumption that every possible thing could become necessary leads to the impossible conclusion that infinite existents would exist all at once, so the assumption is false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever treat a possibility in your life as if it must happen, forgetting that only God is necessary? How does this lesson's proof that not all possibles can become actual challenge you to trust God's order instead of demanding your own? What specific area of your life right now are you presuming necessity where there is only possibility?
?
The argument shows that if everything possible were necessary, there would be no room for order—everything would exist at once. In your own striving and anxieties, are you trying to make every possibility actual, creating chaos? What would it look like to accept the finite, ordered sequence God has placed in your life today?
?
Consider the statement that order in essences is like order in existents. Is your internal life (your thoughts, desires, priorities) ordered like the external world? Repent of any disorder that demands immediacy and submit to the necessary being who alone brings order.
